codecs=&amp;quot;vp8, vorbis&amp;quot;" data-title="Low bandwidth WebM (160P)" data-shorttitle="WebM 160P" data-transcodekey="160p.webm" data-width="214" data-height="160" data-bandwidth="182840" data-framerate="30.833333333333"/&gt;&lt;source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/1/19/AP11_FINAL_APPROACH.ogv/AP11_FINAL_APPROACH.ogv.180p.vp9.webm" type="video/webm; codecs=&amp;quot;vp9, opus&amp;quot;" data-title="Low bandwidth VP9 (180P)" data-shorttitle="VP9 180P" data-transcodekey="180p.vp9.webm" data-width="240" data-height="180" data-bandwidth="177448" data-framerate="30.833333333333"/&gt;&lt;track src="https://commons.wikimedia.org/w/index.php?title=TimedText:AP11_FINAL_APPROACH.ogv.en.srt&amp;amp;action=raw&amp;amp;ctype=text%2Fx-srt" kind="subtitles" type="text/x-srt" srclang="en" label="English (en) subtitles" data-mwtitle="TimedText:AP11_FINAL_APPROACH.ogv.en.srt" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons" data-dir="ltr"/&gt;&lt;/video&gt;&lt;/div&gt;\'><img alt="File:AP11 FINAL APPROACH.ogv" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/AP11_FINAL_APPROACH.ogv/220px--AP11_FINAL_APPROACH.ogv.jpg" style="width:220px;height:165px"/><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/19/AP11_FINAL_APPROACH.ogv" target="new" title="Play media"><span class="play-btn-large"><span class="mw-tmh-playtext">Play media</span></span></a></div> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:AP11_FINAL_APPROACH.ogv" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Landing on the Moon, July 20, 1969</div></div></div>\n<p>ACA was the attitude control assembly, the LM\'s control stick. Output went to the LGC to command the <a href="/wiki/Reaction_control_system" title="Reaction control system">reaction control system</a> (RCS) jets to fire. "Out of Detent" meant that the stick had moved away from its centered position; it was spring-centered like the turn indicator in a car. LGC address 413 contained the variable that indicated that the LM had landed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ALSJ_1_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-ALSJ_1-4">[4]</a></sup>\n</p><p><i>Eagle</i> landed at 20:17:40 UTC on Sunday July 20 with about 25 seconds of fuel left.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ALSJ_1_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-ALSJ_1-4">[4]</a></sup> Apollo 11 landed with less fuel than subsequent missions, and the astronauts encountered a premature low fuel warning. This was later found to be the result of greater propellant \'slosh\' than expected, uncovering a fuel sensor. On subsequent missions, extra anti-slosh baffles were added to the tanks to prevent this.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ALSJ_1_4-3"><a href="#cite_note-ALSJ_1-4">[4]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Armstrong acknowledged Aldrin\'s completion of the post landing checklist with "Engine arm is off", before responding to the CAPCOM, Charles Duke, with the words, "Houston, <a href="/wiki/Tranquility_Base" title="Tranquility Base">Tranquility Base</a> here. The <i>Eagle</i> has landed." Armstrong\'s unrehearsed change of call sign from "Eagle" to "Tranquility Base" emphasized to listeners that landing was complete and successful.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> Duke mispronounced his reply as he expressed the relief at Mission Control: "Roger, Twan&#8212; Tranquility, we copy you on the ground. You got a bunch of guys about to turn blue. We\'re breathing again. Thanks a lot."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ALSJ_1_4-4"><a href="#cite_note-ALSJ_1-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><div class="PopUpMediaTransform" id="mwe_player_2" style="width:220px;" videopayload=\'&lt;div class="mediaContainer" style="width:854px"&gt;&lt;video id="mwe_player_3" poster="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/A_New_Look_at_the_Apollo_11_Landing_Site.ogv/854px--A_New_Look_at_the_Apollo_11_Landing_Site.ogv.jpg" controls="" preload="none" autoplay="" style="width:854px;height:480px" class="kskin" data-durationhint="72.395464852608" data-startoffset="0" data-mwtitle="A_New_Look_at_the_Apollo_11_Landing_Site.ogv" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons"&gt;&lt;source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/cc/A_New_Look_at_the_Apollo_11_Landing_Site.ogv" type="video/ogg; codecs=&amp;quot;vp8, vorbis&amp;quot;" data-title="Small WebM (240P)" data-shorttitle="WebM 240P" data-transcodekey="240p.webm" data-width="426" data-height="240" data-bandwidth="309096" data-framerate="29.97"/&gt;&lt;source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/c/cc/A_New_Look_at_the_Apollo_11_Landing_Site.ogv/A_New_Look_at_the_Apollo_11_Landing_Site.ogv.240p.vp9.webm" type="video/webm; codecs=&amp;quot;vp9, opus&amp;quot;" data-title="Small VP9 (240P)" data-shorttitle="VP9 240P" data-transcodekey="240p.vp9.webm" data-width="426" data-height="240" data-bandwidth="329776" data-framerate="29.97"/&gt;&lt;source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/c/cc/A_New_Look_at_the_Apollo_11_Landing_Site.ogv/A_New_Look_at_the_Apollo_11_Landing_Site.ogv.360p.webm" type="video/webm; codecs=&amp;quot;vp8, vorbis&amp;quot;" data-title="WebM (360P)" data-shorttitle="WebM 360P" data-transcodekey="360p.webm" data-width="640" data-height="360" data-bandwidth="544464" data-framerate="29.97"/&gt;&lt;source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/c/cc/A_New_Look_at_the_Apollo_11_Landing_Site.ogv/A_New_Look_at_the_Apollo_11_Landing_Site.ogv.360p.vp9.webm" type="video/webm; codecs=&amp;quot;vp9, opus&amp;quot;" data-title="VP9 (360P)" data-shorttitle="VP9 360P" data-transcodekey="360p.vp9.webm" data-width="640" data-height="360" data-bandwidth="566736" data-framerate="29.97"/&gt;&lt;/video&gt;&lt;/div&gt;\'><img alt="File:A New Look at the Apollo 11 Landing Site.ogv" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/A_New_Look_at_the_Apollo_11_Landing_Site.ogv/220px--A_New_Look_at_the_Apollo_11_Landing_Site.ogv.jpg" style="width:220px;height:124px"/><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/cc/A_New_Look_at_the_Apollo_11_Landing_Site.ogv" target="new" title="Play media"><span class="play-btn-large"><span class="mw-tmh-playtext">Play media</span></span></a></div> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:A_New_Look_at_the_Apollo_11_Landing_Site.ogv" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Apollo 11 landing site visualized in three dimensions using photography and a stereo digital elevation model from the <a href="/wiki/Lunar_Reconnaissance_Orbiter" title="Lunar Reconnaissance Orbiter">LRO</a> camera.</div></div></div>\n<p>Two and a half hours after landing, before preparations began for the EVA, Aldrin radioed to Earth:\n</p>\n<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>This is the LM pilot. I\'d like to take this opportunity to ask every person listening in, whoever and wherever they may be, to pause for a moment and contemplate the events of the past few hours and to give thanks in his or her own way.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup>\n</p></blockquote>\n<p>He then took <a href="/wiki/Eucharist" title="Eucharist">communion</a> privately. At this time NASA was still fighting a lawsuit brought by atheist <a href="/wiki/Madalyn_Murray_O%27Hair" title="Madalyn Murray O\'Hair">Madalyn Murray O\'Hair</a> (who had objected to the <a href="/wiki/Apollo_8_Genesis_reading" title="Apollo 8 Genesis reading">Apollo 8 crew reading from the Book of Genesis</a>) demanding that their astronauts refrain from broadcasting religious activities while in space. As such, Aldrin chose to refrain from directly mentioning taking communion on the Moon. Aldrin was an elder at the <a href="/wiki/Webster,_Texas" title="Webster, Texas">Webster</a> <a href="/wiki/Presbyterianism" title="Presbyterianism">Presbyterian Church</a>, and his communion kit was prepared by the pastor of the church, Dean Woodruff. Webster Presbyterian possesses the chalice used on the Moon and commemorates the event each year on the Sunday closest to July 20.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChaikin1994204,_623_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChaikin1994204,_623-111">[111]</a></sup> The schedule for the mission called for the astronauts to follow the landing with a five-hour sleep period, but they chose to begin the preparations for the EVA early, thinking that they would be unable to sleep.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEManned_Spacecraft_Center196921&#8211;22_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEManned_Spacecraft_Center196921&#8211;22-112">[112]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lunar_surface_operations">Lunar surface operations</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:As11-40-5886.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="603" data-file-width="738" decoding="async" height="180" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/As11-40-5886.jpg/220px-As11-40-5886.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/As11-40-5886.jpg/330px-As11-40-5886.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/As11-40-5886.jpg/440px-As11-40-5886.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:As11-40-5886.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A photograph of Armstrong taken by Aldrin. This is one of the few photographs of Armstrong on the lunar surface; most of the time he had the camera.</div></div></div>\n<p>Preparations for the EVA began at 23:43.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOrloff2000107_6-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOrloff2000107-6">[6]</a></sup> These took longer than expected; three and a half hours instead of two.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ALSJ_3_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-ALSJ_3-113">[113]</a></sup> During training on Earth, everything required had been neatly laid out in advance, but on the Moon the cabin contained a large number of other items as well, such as checklists, food packets and tools.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEManned_Spacecraft_Center196922_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEManned_Spacecraft_Center196922-114">[114]</a></sup> Once Armstrong and Aldrin were ready to go outside, <i>Eagle</i> was depressurized.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECortright1975215_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECortright1975215-115">[115]</a></sup> The hatch was opened at 02:39:33.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOrloff2000107_6-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOrloff2000107-6">[6]</a></sup> Armstrong initially had some difficulties squeezing through the hatch with his <a href="/wiki/Primary_life_support_system" title="Primary life support system">portable life support system</a> (PLSS).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ALSJ_3_113-1"><a href="#cite_note-ALSJ_3-113">[113]</a></sup> Some of the highest heart rates recorded from Apollo astronauts occurred during LM egress and ingress.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWaligoraHorrigan1975115&#8211;120_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWaligoraHorrigan1975115&#8211;120-116">[116]</a></sup> At 02:51 Armstrong began his descent to the lunar surface. The remote control unit controls on his chest kept him from seeing his feet. Climbing down the nine-rung ladder, Armstrong pulled a D-ring to deploy the modular equipment stowage assembly (MESA) folded against <i>Eagle</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">\'s</span> side and activate the TV camera.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ALSJ_4_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-ALSJ_4-7">[7]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Apollo 11 used <a href="/wiki/Slow-scan_television" title="Slow-scan television">slow-scan television</a> (TV) incompatible with broadcast TV, so it was displayed on a special monitor and a conventional TV camera viewed this monitor, significantly reducing the quality of the picture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Blunder_5_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-Blunder_5-118">[118]</a></sup> The signal was received at <a href="/wiki/Goldstone_Deep_Space_Communications_Complex" title="Goldstone Deep Space Communications Complex">Goldstone</a> in the United States, but with better fidelity by <a href="/wiki/Honeysuckle_Creek_Tracking_Station" title="Honeysuckle Creek Tracking Station">Honeysuckle Creek Tracking Station</a> near <a href="/wiki/Canberra" title="Canberra">Canberra</a> in Australia. Minutes later the feed was switched to the more sensitive <a href="/wiki/Parkes_Observatory" title="Parkes Observatory">Parkes radio telescope</a> in Australia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESarkissian2001287_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESarkissian2001287-119">[119]</a></sup> Despite some technical and weather difficulties, ghostly black and white images of the first lunar EVA were received and broadcast to at least 600 million people on Earth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESarkissian2001287_119-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESarkissian2001287-119">[119]</a></sup> Copies of this video in broadcast format were saved and are widely available, but <a href="/wiki/Apollo_11_missing_tapes" title="Apollo 11 missing tapes">recordings of the original slow scan source transmission from the lunar surface</a> were likely destroyed during routine magnetic tape re-use at NASA.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Blunder_5_118-1"><a href="#cite_note-Blunder_5-118">[118]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Apollo_11_plaque_closeup_on_Moon.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="822" data-file-width="873" decoding="async" height="207" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Apollo_11_plaque_closeup_on_Moon.jpg/220px-Apollo_11_plaque_closeup_on_Moon.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Apollo_11_plaque_closeup_on_Moon.jpg/330px-Apollo_11_plaque_closeup_on_Moon.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Apollo_11_plaque_closeup_on_Moon.jpg/440px-Apollo_11_plaque_closeup_on_Moon.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Apollo_11_plaque_closeup_on_Moon.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Lunar_plaque" title="Lunar plaque">The plaque</a> left on the ladder of <i>Eagle</i></div></div></div>\n<table class="mbox-small noprint" role="presentation" style="background-color:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;color:#000;">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td class="mbox-image"><div
